- [Spectacled caiman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spectacled_caiman "Spectacled caiman") (*[Caiman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caimaninae "Caimaninae") crocodilus*)[^211]
- †*[Purussaurus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purussaurus "Purussaurus")*[^212] – giant caimans

**Birds**

- [Great curassow](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_curassow "Great curassow") (*Crax rubra*)[^pereira2004-213]
- [Toucans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toucan "Toucan") (Ramphastidae)
- [Tinamous](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tinamou "Tinamou") (Tinamidae)
- Additional [suboscine birds](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suboscine_bird "Suboscine bird") (Tyranni):
- [Gnateaters](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gnateater "Gnateater") (Conopophagidae)[^weirbermingham2009-201]
- [Cotingas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cotinga "Cotinga") (Cotingidae)[^weirbermingham2009-201]
- [Ground antbirds](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ground_antbird "Ground antbird") (Formicariidae)[^weirbermingham2009-201]
- [Ovenbirds](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ovenbird_\(family\) "Ovenbird (family)") and [woodcreepers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woodcreeper "Woodcreeper") (Furnariidae)[^irestedt2002-214]
- [Antpittas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antpitta "Antpitta") (Grallariidae)[^weirbermingham2009-201]
- [Manakins](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manakin "Manakin") (Pipridae)[^weirbermingham2009-201]
- [Tapaculos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tapaculo "Tapaculo") (Rhinocryptidae)[^weirbermingham2009-201]
- [Antbirds](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antbird "Antbird") (Thamnophilidae)[^weirbermingham2009-201]
- Other [Neotropical parrots](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neotropical_parrot "Neotropical parrot") (Arinae)

**Mammals**

- Other [opossums](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opossum "Opossum") (Didelphidae) – 11 additional extant species[^calisting-148]
- Xenarthrans (Xenarthra)
- [Northern naked-tailed armadillo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_naked-tailed_armadillo "Northern naked-tailed armadillo") (*Cabassous centralis*)
- [Three-toed sloths](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three-toed_sloth "Three-toed sloth") (Bradypodidae: [*Bradypus variegatus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown-throated_three-toed_sloth "Brown-throated three-toed sloth"), [*B. pygmaeus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pygmy_three-toed_sloth "Pygmy three-toed sloth"))
- [Hoffmann's two-toed sloth](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoffmann%27s_two-toed_sloth "Hoffmann's two-toed sloth") (Choloepodidae: *Choloepus hoffmanni*)
- †[Scelidotheriid ground sloths](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scelidotheriidae "Scelidotheriidae") (*[Scelidotherium](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scelidotherium "Scelidotherium")*, found in Panama[^scelidopbdb-215])
- [Silky anteater](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silky_anteater "Silky anteater") (Cyclopedidae: *Cyclopes dorsalis*)
- Other [anteaters](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myrmecophagidae "Myrmecophagidae") (Myrmecophagidae: [*Myrmecophaga tridactyla*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giant_anteater "Giant anteater"),[^217] [*Tamandua mexicana*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamandua "Tamandua"))
- Rodents (Rodentia)
- [Rothschild's](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rothschild%27s_porcupine "Rothschild's porcupine") and [Mexican hairy dwarf](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_hairy_dwarf_porcupine "Mexican hairy dwarf porcupine") [porcupines](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_World_porcupine "New World porcupine") (*Coendou rothschildi*, *Sphiggurus mexicanus*)
- Other [caviomorph rodents](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caviomorpha "Caviomorpha") (Caviomorpha) – 9 additional extant species[^calisting-148]
- [Platyrrhine monkeys](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_World_monkey "New World monkey") (Platyrrhini) – at least 8 extant species[^calisting-148][^219]
- Carnivorans (Carnivora)
- [Olingos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olingo "Olingo") (*Bassaricyon*) – thought to have arisen in the Andes of northwest South America after their procyonid ancestors invaded from the north, before diversifying and migrating back to Central America[^helgen2013-220]
- South American short-faced bears ([Tremarctinae](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tremarctinae "Tremarctinae"): †*[Arctotherium wingei](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctotherium_wingei "Arctotherium wingei")*) – thought to have invaded to as far as the [Yucatán](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula "Yucatán Peninsula") after arising in South America from North American ancestors[^schubert2019-221]
- South American canids ([Caninae](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caninae "Caninae"): †*[Protocyon troglodytes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protocyon_troglodytes "Protocyon troglodytes")*) – thought to have invaded to as far as the [Yucatán](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula "Yucatán Peninsula") after arising in South America from North American ancestors[^schubert2019-221]
- Bats (Chiroptera)
- [Emballonurid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emballonuridae "Emballonuridae") bats[^teeling2005-67]
- [Furipterid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Furipteridae "Furipteridae") bats[^gunnell2014-66] (*[Furipterus horrens](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Furipterus_horrens "Furipterus horrens")*)
- Other [mormoopid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mormoopidae "Mormoopidae") bats[^gunnell2014-66]
- [Noctilionid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noctilionidae "Noctilionidae") bats[^gunnell2014-66] (*[Noctilio albiventris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noctilio_albiventris "Noctilio albiventris")*, *[Noctilio leporinus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noctilio_leporinus "Noctilio leporinus")*)
- Other [phyllostomid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phyllostomidae "Phyllostomidae") bats,[^gunnell2014-66] including all 3 extant [vampire bat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vampire_bat "Vampire bat") species (Desmodontinae)
- [Thyropterid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thyropteridae "Thyropteridae") bats[^gunnell2014-66] (*[Thyroptera discifera](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thyroptera_discifera "Thyroptera discifera")*, *[Thyroptera tricolor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thyroptera_tricolor "Thyroptera tricolor")*)

## List of South American species of North American origin

Extant or extinct (†) South American taxa whose ancestors migrated out of North America:[^qualifier-196]

**Amphibians**

- [Dermophiid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dermophiidae "Dermophiidae") [caecilians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caecilian "Caecilian") (*[Dermophis glandulosus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dermophis_glandulosus "Dermophis glandulosus")*) – only present in northwestern Colombia[^savage2001-222]
- [Lungless salamanders](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lungless_salamander "Lungless salamander")[^224][^early_amphibians-209] (*[Bolitoglossa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolitoglossa "Bolitoglossa")*,[^elmer2013-223][^225] *[Oedipina](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oedipina "Oedipina")*) – only present in northern South America
- [Ranid frogs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ranidae "Ranidae")[^webb-197] – only present in northern South America

**Reptiles**

- Turtles (Testudines)
- [Chelydrid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chelydridae "Chelydridae") (snapping) turtles (*[Chelydra acutirostris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chelydra_acutirostris "Chelydra acutirostris")*) – only present in northwestern South America
- [Emydid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emydidae "Emydidae") (pond) turtles (*[Trachemys](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trachemys "Trachemys")*)
- [Geoemydid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoemydidae "Geoemydidae") (wood) turtles (*[Rhinoclemmys](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhinoclemmys "Rhinoclemmys")*)[^226] – only present in northern South America
- Snakes (Serpentes)
- [Coral snakes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coral_snake "Coral snake") (*[Leptomicrurus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leptomicrurus "Leptomicrurus")*, *[Micrurus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Micrurus "Micrurus")*)[^227][^228]
- South American [rattlesnake](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rattlesnake "Rattlesnake") (*[Crotalus durissus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crotalus_durissus "Crotalus durissus")*)[^229]
- Lanceheads (*[Bothrops](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bothrops "Bothrops")*)
- Bushmasters (*[Lachesis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lachesis_\(genus\) "Lachesis (genus)")*)
- Other [pit vipers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crotalinae "Crotalinae") (*[Bothriechis schlegelii](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bothriechis_schlegelii "Bothriechis schlegelii")*, *[Bothriopsis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bothriopsis "Bothriopsis")*, *[Porthidium](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porthidium "Porthidium")*)[^230]

**Birds**

- [American sparrows](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_sparrow "American sparrow") (Emberizidae)[^weirbermingham2009-201][^ericsonchristidis2002-231]
- [Trogons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trogon "Trogon") (*[Trogon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trogon_\(genus\) "Trogon (genus)")*)[^232]
- [Condors](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Condor "Condor") (*[Vultur gryphus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andean_condor "Andean condor")*, †*[Dryornis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dryornis "Dryornis")*, †*[Geronogyps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geronogyps&action=edit&redlink=1 "Geronogyps (page does not exist)")*, †*[Wingegyps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wingegyps "Wingegyps")*, †*[Perugyps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Perugyps&action=edit&redlink=1 "Perugyps (page does not exist)")*)[^233][^hadrogyps-234][^condor-235][^236]

**Mammals**

- [Small-eared shrews](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small-eared_shrew "Small-eared shrew") (*Cryptotis*) – only present in NW South America: Colombia, Venezuela, Ecuador, Peru
- Rodents (Rodentia)
- [Geomyid pocket gophers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pocket_gopher "Pocket gopher") (*[Orthogeomys thaeleri](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thaeler%27s_pocket_gopher "Thaeler's pocket gopher")*) – one species, in Colombia
- [Heteromyid mice](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heteromyidae "Heteromyidae") (*[Heteromys](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heteromys "Heteromys")*) – only present in NW South America: Colombia, Venezuela, Ecuador
- [Cricetid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_World_rats_and_mice "New World rats and mice") – primarily [sigmodontine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigmodontinae "Sigmodontinae") – rats and mice (Cricetidae: Sigmodontinae) – the nonsigmodontines consist of two species present only in Colombia and Ecuador[^237]
- Tree [squirrels](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sciuridae "Sciuridae") (*[Sciurus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sciurus "Sciurus")*, *[Microsciurus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsciurus "Microsciurus")*, *[Sciurillus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neotropical_pygmy_squirrel "Neotropical pygmy squirrel")*) – present in northern and central South America
- [Cottontail](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cottontail_rabbit "Cottontail rabbit") [rabbits](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rabbit "Rabbit") ([*Sylvilagus brasiliensis*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tapeti "Tapeti"), [*S. floridanus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_cottontail "Eastern cottontail"), [*S. varynaensis*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venezuelan_lowland_rabbit "Venezuelan lowland rabbit")) – present in northern and central South America
- Odd-toed ungulates (Perissodactyla)
- [Tapirs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tapir "Tapir") ([*Tapirus bairdii*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baird%27s_tapir "Baird's tapir"), †[*T. cristatellus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tapirus_cristatellus "Tapirus cristatellus"), [*T. pinchaque*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_tapir "Mountain tapir"), †[*T. rondoniensis*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tapirus_rondoniensis "Tapirus rondoniensis"), [*T. terrestris*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brazilian_tapir "Brazilian tapir"))
- [Equids](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equidae "Equidae") (*[Equus ferus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equus_ferus "Equus ferus")*, †*[Hippidion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippidion "Hippidion")*)[^240]

- [Deer](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deer "Deer") (†*[Antifer](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antifer "Antifer")*, †*[Morenelaphus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morenelaphus "Morenelaphus")*, †*[Agalmaceros](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agalmaceros "Agalmaceros")*, [*Odocoileus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/White-tailed_deer "White-tailed deer"), [*Blastocerus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marsh_deer "Marsh deer"), [*Ozotoceros*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pampas_deer "Pampas deer"), [*Mazama*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brocket_deer "Brocket deer"), [*Pudu*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pud%C3%BA "Pudú"), *[Hippocamelus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippocamelus "Hippocamelus")*)
- [Camelids](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camelid "Camelid") ([*Lama guanicoe*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guanaco "Guanaco"), [*Vicugna vicugna*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vicu%C3%B1a "Vicuña"), †*[Eulamaops](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eulamaops "Eulamaops")*, †*[Hemiauchenia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemiauchenia "Hemiauchenia")*, †*[Palaeolama](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palaeolama "Palaeolama")*)
- †[Gomphotheres](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gomphothere "Gomphothere") (*[Cuvieronius](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuvieronius "Cuvieronius") hyodon*, *[Notiomastodon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Notiomastodon "Notiomastodon")*[^242] *platensis*) – [elephant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elephant "Elephant") relatives[^moth%c3%a92017-91]
- Carnivorans (Carnivora)

- Other [mustelids](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustelidae "Mustelidae") ([Mustelinae](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustelinae "Mustelinae"): *[Eira](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tayra "Tayra")*, *[Galictis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galictis "Galictis")*, *[Lyncodon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patagonian_weasel "Patagonian weasel")*, *[Neogale](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neogale "Neogale")*)
- [Hog-nosed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hog-nosed_skunk "Hog-nosed skunk") [skunks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skunk "Skunk") (*[Conepatus chinga](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molina%27s_hog-nosed_skunk "Molina's hog-nosed skunk")*, *[C. humboldtii](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt%27s_hog-nosed_skunk "Humboldt's hog-nosed skunk")*, *[C. semistriatus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Striped_hog-nosed_skunk "Striped hog-nosed skunk")*)
- [Procyonids](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procyonidae "Procyonidae") (*[Procyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procyon_\(genus\) "Procyon (genus)")*, [*Nasua*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coati "Coati"), [*Nasuella*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_coati "Mountain coati"), [*Potos*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinkajou "Kinkajou"), [*Bassaricyon*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olingo "Olingo"), †*[Cyonasua](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyonasua "Cyonasua")*, †*[Chapalmalania](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chapalmalania "Chapalmalania")*)
- [Short-faced bears](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctodus "Arctodus") ([Tremarctinae](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tremarctinae "Tremarctinae"): [*Tremarctos ornatus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spectacled_bear "Spectacled bear"), †*[Arctotherium](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctotherium "Arctotherium")*)[^243]
- [Wolves](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canis#Coyotes,_jackals,_and_wolves "Canis") (†*Canis gezi*, †*[C. nehringi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canis_nehringi "Canis nehringi")*, †*[A. dirus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dire_wolf "Dire wolf")* – the latter known only from as far south as southern Bolivia[^paleobiology_cdirus-244])[^hodnettmead2009-245][^berta1988-246]
- [Gray fox](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_fox "Gray fox")[^247] (*Urocyon cinereoargenteus*) – only present in NW South America: Colombia, Venezuela
- Other [canids](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canids "Canids") (†*[Dusicyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dusicyon "Dusicyon")*,[^httpwwwsciencedailycomreleaseshtm-248][^cooper-249] †*[Theriodictis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theriodictis "Theriodictis")*, †*[Protocyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protocyon "Protocyon")*, [*Atelocynus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short-eared_dog "Short-eared dog"), [*Cerdocyon*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crab-eating_fox "Crab-eating fox"), *[Lycalopex](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lycalopex "Lycalopex")*, [*Chrysocyon*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maned_wolf "Maned wolf"), [*Speothos*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bush_dog "Bush dog"))
- Small [felids](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felidae "Felidae") (*[Leopardus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leopardus "Leopardus")*) – all 9 extant species (e.g. [*L. pardalis*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocelot "Ocelot"), [*L. wiedii*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margay "Margay"))
- [Cougar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cougar "Cougar") (*Puma concolor*) and [jaguarundi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaguarundi "Jaguarundi") (*P. yagouaroundi)*
- [Jaguar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaguar "Jaguar") (*Panthera onca*)
- †Scimitar cats (*[Xenosmilus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenosmilus "Xenosmilus")*, *[Homotherium](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homotherium "Homotherium")*) – known so far only from Uruguay[^mones2004-250] and Venezuela[^251][^252][^rinc%c3%b3nprevosti2011-253]
- †[Saber-toothed cats](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smilodon "Smilodon") (*Smilodon gracilis*,[^rinc%c3%b3nprevosti2011-253] *S. fatalis*,[^manzuetti2018-254] *S. populator*)
- †[American lion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_lion "American lion") (*Panthera leo atrox*), reported from Peru[^kurt%c3%a9n1980-255] and Argentina and Chile;[^chimento2017-256] however, the former set of remains has later been identified as belonging to a jaguar[^257] and the latter set of remains were initially identified as being from jaguars
- Bats (Chiroptera)
- [Natalid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natalidae "Natalidae") bats[^lim2009-65] (*[Chilonatalus micropus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chilonatalus_micropus "Chilonatalus micropus")*, *[Natalus espiritosantensis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natalus_espiritosantensis "Natalus espiritosantensis")*, *[N. tumidirostris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natalus_tumidirostris "Natalus tumidirostris")*)
- [Vespertilionid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vespertilionidae "Vespertilionidae") bats[^lim2009-65]

- Amazonian palm viper, *[Bothrops bilineatus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bothrops_bilineatus "Bothrops bilineatus")*

[^22]: During the [Eocene](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eocene "Eocene"), astrapotheres[^bond2011-19] and litopterns[^bond2006-20][^gelfo2015-21] were also present in Antarctica.

[^26]: Sequencing of [collagen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collagen "Collagen") from fossils of one recently extinct species each of notoungulates and litopterns has indicated that these orders comprise a [sister group](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sister_group "Sister group") to the [perissodactyls](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perissodactyl "Perissodactyl").[^welkercollins2015-23][^buckley2015-24] Mitochondrial DNA obtained from *[Macrauchenia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macrauchenia "Macrauchenia")* corroborates this and gives an estimated divergence date of 66 Ma ago.[^westbury2017-25]

[^29]: Once in Australia, facing less competition, marsupials diversified to fill a much larger array of niches than in South America, where they were largely carnivorous.

[^30]: It is the [sister group](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sister_group "Sister group") to a [clade](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clade "Clade") containing all other extant australidelphians (roughly 238 species).

[^39]: Ziphodont (lateromedially compressed, recurved and serrated) teeth tend to arise in terrestrial crocodilians because, unlike their aquatic cousins, they are unable to dispatch their prey by simply holding them underwater and drowning them; they thus need cutting teeth with which to slice open their victims.

[^64]: It is also notable that both [simians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simian "Simian") (ancestral to monkeys) and [hystricognath](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hystricognathi "Hystricognathi") rodents (ancestral to caviomorphs) are believed to have arrived in Africa by rafting from Eurasia about 40 Ma ago.[^chaimanee-63]

[^68]: North American [gopher tortoises](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gopherus "Gopherus") are most closely related to the Asian genus *[Manouria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manouria "Manouria")*.

[^78]: An alternative explanation blames climatic and physiographic changes associated with the uplift of the Andes.[^gasparini-43]

[^97]: Of the 6 families of North American rodents that did not originate in South America, only [beavers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beaver "Beaver") and [mountain beavers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_beaver "Mountain beaver") failed to migrate to South America. (However, human-introduced beavers have become serious [pests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pest_\(organism\) "Pest (organism)") in [Tierra del Fuego](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego "Tierra del Fuego").)

[^102]: In this connection, however, [chalicotheres](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalicothere "Chalicothere"), clawed perissodactyl herbivores ecologically similar to ground sloths, died out in North America in the Miocene about 9 Ma ago, while they survived to the early Pleistocene in Asia and Africa.[^amnh_chalicotheriidae-101]

[^105]: Simpson, 1950, p. 382[^simpson_history_1950-104]

[^106]: Marshall, 1988, p. 386[^landmammals-5]

[^107]: Of the 11 extant families of South American caviomorph rodents, five are present in Central America; only two of these, [Erethizontidae](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_World_porcupine "New World porcupine") and [Caviidae](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caviidae "Caviidae"), ever reached North America. (The [nutria/coypu](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coypu "Coypu") has been introduced to a number of North American locales.)

[^110]: P. S. Martin (2005), pp. 30–37, 119.[^martin-109] The figure of 25 South American megaherbivore species breaks down as follows: four gomphotheres, two camelids, nine ground sloths, five glyptodonts, and five toxodontids. This can be compared to Africa's present and recent total of six megaherbivores: one giraffe, one hippo, two rhinos, and two elephants (considering the [African forest elephant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loxodonta_cyclotis "Loxodonta cyclotis") as a separate species).

[^canidlisting-113]: The [extant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extant_taxon "Extant taxon") [canid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canid "Canid") and [cervid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cervid "Cervid") genera by continent are as follows: **Canid genera by continent**

- North America: 3 genera, 9 species – *[Canis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canis "Canis")*, *[Urocyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urocyon "Urocyon")*, *[Vulpes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulpes "Vulpes")*
- Central America: 3 genera, 4 species – *[Canis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canis "Canis")*, *[Speothos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speothos "Speothos")*, *[Urocyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urocyon "Urocyon")*
- South America: 6 genera, 11 species – *[Atelocynus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atelocynus "Atelocynus")*, *[Cerdocyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerdocyon "Cerdocyon")*, *[Chrysocyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chrysocyon "Chrysocyon")*, *[Lycalopex](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lycalopex "Lycalopex")*, *[Speothos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speothos "Speothos")*, *[Urocyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urocyon "Urocyon")*
- Eurasia: 4 genera, 12 species – *[Canis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canis "Canis")*, *[Cuon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuon "Cuon")*, *[Nyctereutes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nyctereutes "Nyctereutes")*, *[Vulpes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulpes "Vulpes")*
- Africa: 4 genera, 12 species – *[Canis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canis "Canis")*, *[Lycaon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lycaon_\(genus\) "Lycaon (genus)")*, *[Otocyon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otocyon "Otocyon")*, *[Vulpes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulpes "Vulpes")*

**Cervid genera by continent**

- North America: 4 genera, 5 species – *[Alces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alces "Alces")*, *[Cervus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cervus "Cervus")*, *[Odocoileus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odocoileus "Odocoileus")*, *[Rangifer](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reindeer "Reindeer")*
- Central America: 2 genera, 4 species – *[Mazama](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brocket_deer "Brocket deer")*, *[Odocoileus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odocoileus "Odocoileus")*
- South America: 6 genera, 16 species – *[Blastocerus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blastocerus "Blastocerus")*, *[Hippocamelus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippocamelus "Hippocamelus")*, *[Mazama](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brocket_deer "Brocket deer")*, *[Odocoileus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odocoileus "Odocoileus")*, *[Ozotoceros](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ozotoceros "Ozotoceros")*, *[Pudu](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pud%C3%BA "Pudú")*
- Eurasia: 10 genera, 36 species – *[Alces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alces "Alces")*, *[Axis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_\(genus\) "Axis (genus)")*, *[Capreolus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capreolus "Capreolus")*, *[Cervus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cervus "Cervus")*, *[Dama](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fallow_deer "Fallow deer")*, *[Elaphodus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elaphodus "Elaphodus")*, *[Elaphurus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elaphurus "Elaphurus")*, *[Hydropotes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydropotes "Hydropotes")*, *[Muntiacus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muntiacus "Muntiacus")*, *[Rangifer](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reindeer "Reindeer")*
- Africa: 1 genus, 1 species – *[Cervus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cervus "Cervus")*

[^117]: Including extinct genera, South America has hosted nine genera of cervids, eight genera of mustelids, and 10 genera of canids. However, some of this diversity of South American forms apparently arose in North or Central America prior to the interchange.[^gaipatterns-98] Significant disagreement exists in the literature concerning how much of the diversification of South America's canids occurred prior to the invasions. A number of studies concur that the grouping of endemic South American canids (excluding *Urocyon* and *Canis*, although sometimes transferring *C. gezi* to the South American group[^prevosti2010-114]) is a clade.[^prevosti2010-114][^perinirusso2010-115][^slaterthalmann2009-116] However, different authors conclude that members of this clade reached South America in at least two,[^perinirusso2010-115] three to four,[^prevosti2010-114] or six[^slaterthalmann2009-116] invasions from North America.

[^118]: *Canis*, e.g. *[Canis dirus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canis_dirus "Canis dirus")*, was present in South America until the end of the Pleistocene.

[^calisting-148]: The Central American species of South American origin ([opossums](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opossum "Opossum"), [xenarthrans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenarthra "Xenarthra"), [caviomorph rodents](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caviomorph_rodent "Caviomorph rodent") and [platyrrhine monkeys](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Platyrrhine_monkey "Platyrrhine monkey")) are as follows: **Central American opossum species**

- [Derby's woolly opossum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Derby%27s_woolly_opossum "Derby's woolly opossum") (*Caluromys derbianus*)

[^149]: During the [Miocene](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miocene "Miocene") alone, between about 23 and 5 Ma ago, 11 episodes of invasions of North America from Eurasia have been recognized, bringing a total of 81 new genera into North America.[^gaipatterns-98]

[^150]: The combination of Africa, Eurasia and North America was termed the "World Continent" by [George Gaylord Simpson](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Gaylord_Simpson "George Gaylord Simpson").[^simpson_history_1950-104]

[^151]: Simpson, 1950, p. 368[^simpson_history_1950-104]

[^157]: According to data on the [EQ](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain_to_body_mass_ratio "Brain to body mass ratio") (encephalization quotient, a measure of the brain to body size ratio adjusted for the expected effect of differences in body size) of fossil ungulates compiled by H. Jerison,[^saungulates-154] North American ungulates showed a trend towards greater EQs going from the [Paleogene](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleogene "Paleogene") to the [Neogene](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neogene "Neogene") periods (average EQs of 0.43 and 0.64, respectively), while the EQs of South American ungulates were static over the same time interval (average EQ unchanged at 0.48).[^ggsimpson-18] This analysis was later criticized.[^radinsky1-155] Jerison subsequently presented data suggesting that native South American ungulates also lagged in the relative size of their [neocortices](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neocortex "Neocortex") (a measurement not subject to the vagaries of body mass estimation).[^jerison2-156] Interestingly, the late survivor *Toxodon* had one of the highest EQ values (0.88) among native Neotropic ungulates.[^radinsky1-155]  
Jerison also found that Neogene xenarthrans had low EQs, similar to those he obtained for South American ungulates.[^saungulates-154]

[^162]: The estimated EQ of *Thylacosmilus atrox*, 0.41 (based on a brain mass of 43.2 g, a body mass of 26.4 kg,[^wroe-158] and an EQ of 43.2/\[0.12\*26400^(2/3)\][^jerison2-156]), is high for a sparassodont,[^quiroga-159] but is lower than that of modern felids, with a mean value of 0.87.[^radinsky2-160] Estimates of 0.38[^jerison_1973-161] and 0.59[^radinsky2-160] have been given for the EQ of much larger *Smilodon fatalis* (based on body mass estimates of 330 and 175 kg, respectively).

[^187]: The [giant tortoises of Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colossochelys_atlas "Colossochelys atlas") and Africa[^tharrison-185] died out much earlier in the [Quaternary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quaternary "Quaternary") than those of South America, Madagascar and Australia, while those of North America[^hansen-186] died out around the same time.

[^194]: P. S. Martin (2005), p. 175.[^martin-109]

[^195]: A number of recently extinct North American (and in some cases also South American) taxa such as tapirs, equids, camelids, [saiga antelope](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saiga_antelope "Saiga antelope"), proboscids, dholes, and lions survived in the Old World, probably mostly for different reasons – tapirs being a likely exception, since their [Old World representative](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malayan_tapir "Malayan tapir") survived only in the rainforests of [Southeast Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia"). (Cheetahs in the broadest sense could be added to this list, although the [New](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_cheetah "American cheetah") and [Old World](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheetah "Cheetah") forms are in different genera.) Old World herbivores may in many cases have been able to learn to be vigilant about the presence of humans during a more gradual appearance (by development or migration) of advanced human hunters in their ranges. In the cases of predators, the Old World representatives in at least some locations would thus have suffered less from extinctions of their prey species. In contrast, the [musk ox](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muskox "Muskox") represents a rare example of a megafaunal taxon that recently became extinct in Asia, but survived in remote areas of [arctic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic "Arctic") North America (its more southerly-distributed relatives, such as the [woodland muskox](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woodland_muskox "Woodland muskox") and [shrub-ox](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shrub-ox "Shrub-ox"), were less fortunate).

[^qualifier-196]: This listing currently has fairly complete coverage of mammals, but only spotty coverage of other groups. Crossings by nonflying mammals and birds occurred during the last 10 [Ma](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annum "Annum"). Crossings by fish, arthropods, rafting amphibians and reptiles, and flying bats and birds were made before 10 Ma ago in many cases. Taxa listed as invasive did not necessarily cross the isthmus themselves; they may have evolved in the adopted land mass from ancestral taxa that made the crossing.

[^206]: *Mixotoxodon* remains have been collected in Central America and Mexico as far north as [Veracruz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veracruz "Veracruz") and [Michoacán](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michoac%C3%A1n "Michoacán"), with a possible find in [Tamaulipas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamaulipas "Tamaulipas");[^mexico-204] additionally, one fossil tooth has been identified in eastern [Texas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas "Texas"), United States.[^lundelius2013-205]

[^208]: Central America is usually defined [physiographically](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_geography "Physical geography") as ending at the [Isthmus of Tehuantepec](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec "Isthmus of Tehuantepec") or less commonly, at the [Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-Mexican_Volcanic_Belt "Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt"). Most of the taxa that proceeded farther but failed to reach the present Mexican border are or were confined to tropical or subtropical climates similar to those of Central America. Examples include the [giant anteater](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myrmecophaga_tridactyla "Myrmecophaga tridactyla"), the [grayish mouse opossum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tlacuatzin_canescens "Tlacuatzin canescens"), the [lowland paca](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuniculus_paca "Cuniculus paca"), and [Geoffroy's spider monkey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ateles_geoffroyi "Ateles geoffroyi").

[^217]: Fossils of the [giant anteater](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myrmecophaga_tridactyla "Myrmecophaga tridactyla") have been found as far north as northwestern [Sonora](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonora "Sonora"), Mexico.[^shaw-216]

[^219]: It has been proposed that monkeys invaded Central America in at least three and probably four waves, as follows: (1) an initial invasion by [*A. pigra*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guatemalan_black_howler "Guatemalan black howler") and [*S. oerstedii*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_American_squirrel_monkey "Central American squirrel monkey") ~ 3 [Ma](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megaannum "Megaannum") ago; (2) an invasion by [*A. palliata*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mantled_howler "Mantled howler") (giving rise to [*A. coibensis*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coiba_Island_howler "Coiba Island howler")), [*A. geoffroyi*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoffroy%27s_spider_monkey "Geoffroy's spider monkey") and [*C. capucinus*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/White-headed_capuchin "White-headed capuchin") ~ 2 Ma ago; an invasion by [*A. zonalis*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panamanian_night_monkey "Panamanian night monkey") and [*S. geoffroyi*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoffroy%27s_tamarin "Geoffroy's tamarin") ~ 1 Ma ago; a most recent invasion by [*A. fusciceps*](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black-headed_spider_monkey "Black-headed spider monkey"). The species of the first wave have apparently been out-competed by those of the second, and now have much more restricted distributions.[^218]

[^224]: [Salamanders](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salamander "Salamander") apparently dispersed to South America by the Early Miocene, about 23 [Ma](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annum "Annum") ago.[^elmer2013-223] Nevertheless, the salamander fauna of South America, which is restricted to the tropical region, consists of only 2 clades, and has fewer species and is far less diverse than that of much smaller Central America. Salamanders are believed to have originated in northern [Pangea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pangea "Pangea"), perhaps not long before it separated to become [Laurasia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laurasia "Laurasia"),[^early_amphibians-209] and are not present anywhere else in the [Southern Hemisphere](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere "Southern Hemisphere") (see the [world salamander distribution map](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cypron-Range_Caudata.svg "File:Cypron-Range Caudata.svg")). In contrast, [caecilians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caecilian "Caecilian") have a mostly [Gondwanan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gondwana "Gondwana") [distribution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Distribution.gymnophiona.2.png "File:Distribution.gymnophiona.2.png"). Apart from a small region of overlap in southern China and northern Southeast Asia, Central America and northern South America are the only places in the world where both salamanders and caecilians are present.

[^236]: Condors apparently reached South America by the late Miocene or early Pliocene (4.5 – 6.0 Ma ago), several million years before the formation of the isthmus.[^condor-235] Condor-like forms in North America date back to the [Barstovian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miocene#North_America "Miocene") [stage](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stage_\(stratigraphy\) "Stage (stratigraphy)") (middle Miocene, 11.8 – 15.5 Ma ago).[^hadrogyps-234]

[^237]: This is based on the definition of Sigmodontinae that excludes [Neotominae](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neotominae "Neotominae") and [Tylomyinae](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tylomyinae "Tylomyinae").

[^240]: *[Hippidion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippidion "Hippidion")*, a relatively short-legged equid that developed in South America after invading from North America about 2.5 [Ma](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annum "Annum") ago, has traditionally been thought to have evolved from [pliohippines](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolution_of_the_horse#Pliohippus "Evolution of the horse").[^evolution-238][^ancientdna-239] However, recent studies of the [DNA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA "DNA") of *Hippidion* and other [New World](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_World "New World") Pleistocene horses indicate that *Hippidion* is actually a member of *[Equus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equus_\(genus\) "Equus (genus)")*, closely related to the [extant horse](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wild_horse "Wild horse"), *E. ferus*.[^evolution-238][^ancientdna-239] Another invasion of South America by *Equus* occurred about one Ma ago, and this lineage, traditionally viewed as the subgenus *Equus (Amerhippus)*, appears indistinguishable from *E. ferus*.[^ancientdna-239] Both these lineages became extinct at the end of the Pleistocene, but *E. ferus* was reintroduced from Eurasia by Europeans in the 16th century. Note: the authors of the DNA sequence study of *Equus (Amerhippus)* use "*E. caballus*" as an alternative specific name for "*E. ferus*".[^ancientdna-239]

[^242]: Not to be confused with the [American mastodon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_mastodon "American mastodon") (*Mammut americanum*), a proboscid from a different family whose remains have been found no further south than [Honduras](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honduras "Honduras").[^241]

[^247]: Not to be confused with the [South American gray fox](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_American_gray_fox "South American gray fox").

1. [**<sup>^</sup>**](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/#ref_Anone) The native South American ungulates dwindled gradually as North American ungulates invaded and diversified. The changes in number and composition of South America's ungulate genera over time are given in the table below. The [Quaternary extinction event](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quaternary_extinction_event "Quaternary extinction event") that delivered the *[coup de grâce](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coup_de_gr%C3%A2ce "Coup de grâce")* to the native Neotropic ungulates also dealt a heavy blow to South America's ungulate immigrants.
